## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, which is the standard continuous-time population dynamics setup. Typical models express dP_dt as P times a per-capita growth term that depends on density (P) and/or external forcing over time (t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, constant per-capita rate)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant inflow/outflow added to intrinsic growth)
- Density-dependent linear per-capita rate: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P) (crowding reduces growth when c1 < 0)
- Carrying-capacity-limited growth (Verhulst-type ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (single stable equilibrium at P = 1/c1 when parameters positive)
- Theta-logistic generalization: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence via c2)
- Gompertz-type regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with log density dependence; asymptote near P = c1)
- Allee effect (strong) model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (reduced growth at low density; threshold near P = 1/c2)
- Saturating density limitation (rational form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) / (1 + c2 * P)) (crowding effect that saturates at high P)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (external removal independent of population size)
- Proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (removal proportional to P; reduces effective growth rate)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)))) (seasonal resource availability via K(t))
- Pulse disturbance / boom-bust forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * exp(-c3 * (t - c4) ** 2) (transient event affecting growth around time c4)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth representation: writing dP_dt = P * g(t, P) helps interpret g as the per-individual net rate; many ecological mechanisms act through g.
- Equilibria from factorization: forms like dP_dt = P * (a - b*P) or dP_dt = P*(a - b*P)*(c*P - 1) reveal zero-growth steady states and thresholds directly.
- Allee threshold behavior: inclusion of a factor (c*P - 1) (or similar) creates negative growth at low P and bistability (extinction vs persistence).
- Saturating crowding effects: rational-in-P modifiers (e.g., (c1*P)/(1+c2*P)) model limits where additional density has diminishing marginal impact.
- External removals: subtracting c (constant yield) or c*P (proportional harvest) shifts equilibria and can induce collapse even when intrinsic growth is positive.
- Seasonality/forcing: sin(c*t + phase) terms indicate periodic environments; they can create oscillatory P(t) even without predator-prey coupling.
- Changing resource base: making the effective carrying capacity depend on t (e.g., via 1 + c*sin(c*t)) encodes habitat/food fluctuations and produces time-dependent stable levels.
- Disturbance events: localized exp(-c*(t-t0)^2) additions approximate shocks (e.g., temporary stocking, outbreak, disaster) concentrated around a specific time.

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4 + c5*P*exp(-c6*t)
Candidate formulas: 52

GT (fixed):
\[
0.712449\, (1-\tfrac{P}{68.906009})P\;+\;0.712449\,P^{1/3}\;+\;0.712449\,P\,e^{-0.03459336\,t}
\]
Expand the polynomial part:
\[
0.712449\,P\;-\;\frac{0.712449}{68.906009}P^2\;+\;0.712449\,P^{1/3}\;+\;0.712449\,P\,e^{-0.03459336 t}
\]
So GT is exactly a sum of four independent basis terms: \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), \(P\), and \(P e^{kt}\) with \(k<0\). No other \(t\)-dependence and no extra nonlinear-in-\(P\) functions (log, sin, Abs, rational, etc.).

Now check candidates: a candidate can match iff we can set its parameters so that (i) it contains these four terms with correct coefficients/exponent, and (ii) any extra terms are forced to vanish (by setting their coefficients to 0) or reduce identically to 0 for all \(P,t\).

1. Has required \(P^{1/3},P^2,P,P e^{c4 t}\). Extra term \(c5\exp(c6\sin(\cdot))\) can be killed by \(c5=0\). Set \(c0=0.712449\), \(c1=-0.712449/68.906009\), \(c2=0.712449\), \(c3=0.712449\), \(c4=-0.03459336\). **Matches.**

2. Same core terms; extra \(c5\sin(Pc6+c7)\) killed by \(c5=0\). Choose remaining constants as in (1). **Matches.**

3. Same core terms; extra trig product killed by \(c5=0\). Choose remaining constants as in (1). **Matches.**

4. Form: \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2 e^{c3 t} + P^{c4}c5 + c6\log(\cdot)\). Kill log with \(c6=0\). Set \(c4=1/3\), \(c5=0.712449\), \(c0=-0.712449/68.906009\), \(c1=0.712449\), \(c2=0.712449\), \(c3=-0.03459336\). **Matches.**

5. Has core terms; extra \(P c5\log(1+c6/P)\) cannot be made identically 0 for all \(P\) unless \(c5=0\) (since log term depends on \(P\)). Set \(c5=0\), then choose constants as in (1). **Matches.**

6. Same: kill \(c5\log(Pc6+1)\) by \(c5=0\). Then set constants as in (1). **Matches.**

7. Contains \(P^{1/3}c0\), \(P^2 c1\), linear \(P\) terms, and \(P c6 e^{c7 t}\). The weird term \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}\) can be removed by \(c2=0\). Also there are multiple linear \(P\) terms \(P*c5 + P*c8\) that can sum to the needed linear coefficient. Set \(c0=0.712449\), \(c1=-0.712449/68.906009\), \(c6=0.712449\), \(c7=-0.03459336\), and choose \(c5,c8\) so \(c5+c8=0.712449\). **Matches.**

8. Has \(P^{1/3}\) and an exponential linear-in-\(P\) term, but polynomial powers are \(P^3\) and \(P^2\) and multiple \(P^2\) terms. We could set \(c1=0\) to remove \(P^3\), and combine \(P^2\) coefficients to match the needed \(P^2\). Linear \(P\) terms can match too. So yes: set \(c1=0\); choose \(c2+c3+c4=-0.712449/68.906009\); choose \(c5+c6=0.712449\); set \(c7=0.712449\), \(c8=-0.03459336\); set \(c0=0.712449\). **Matches.**

9. Includes \(\text{Abs}(P)\) and a pure \(e^{c7 t}\) term \(c8 e^{c7 t}\). To match GT (which has no \(|P|\) and no pure \(e^{kt}\) term), must set \(c6=0\) and \(c8=0\). Then it reduces to polynomial + \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}+P*c5\). But then there is **no** \(P^{1/3}\) term and no \(P e^{kt}\) term. Cannot match. **No.**

10. Similar to 9 but without Abs/pure exp. Still lacks \(P^{1/3}\) term. Also has \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}\) which could create \(P^{1/3}\) only if exponent makes it \(P^{1/3}\), but it is \(P^{1+c4}\) times constants, so to get \(P^{1/3}\) would need \(1+c4=1/3\Rightarrow c4=-2/3\), producing \(P^{1/3}\) but then it is multiplied by \(P\) already? Actually term is \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}=c2*c3^{c4} P^{1+c4}\). Yes could yield \(P^{1/3}\) with \(c4=-2/3\).
